**Poland**,[^3] officially the **Republic of Poland**,[^4] is a country in [Central Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe"). It extends from the [Baltic Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea") in the north to the [Sudetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudetes "Sudetes") and [Carpathian Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains "Carpathian Mountains") in the south, and borders [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania "Lithuania") and [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia") [^5] to the northeast; [Belarus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarus "Belarus") and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") to the east; [Slovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovakia "Slovakia") and the [Czech Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czech_Republic "Czech Republic") to the south; and [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany") to the west. The territory has a varied landscape, diverse ecosystems, and a [temperate climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_climate "Temperate climate"). Poland is composed of sixteen [voivodeships](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voivodeships_of_Poland "Voivodeships of Poland") and is the fifth most populous [member state of the European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union "Member state of the European Union") (EU), with over 38 million people, and the [fifth largest EU country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_area "List of European countries by area") by land area, covering 312,696 km <sup>2</sup> (120,733 sq mi). The capital and [largest city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Poland "List of cities and towns in Poland") is [Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw"); other major cities include [Kraków](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków"), [Wrocław](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw "Wrocław"), [Łódź](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA "Łódź"), [Poznań](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pozna%C5%84 "Poznań"), and [Gdańsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk "Gdańsk").

[Prehistoric human activity on Polish soil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_and_protohistory_of_Poland "Prehistory and protohistory of Poland") dates to the [Lower Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic "Lower Paleolithic"), with continuous settlement since the end of the [Last Glacial Period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_Glacial_Period "Last Glacial Period"). Culturally diverse throughout [late antiquity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_antiquity "Late antiquity"), in the [early medieval period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages "Early Middle Ages") the region became inhabited by the [West Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Slavs "West Slavs") tribal [Polans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polans_\(western\) "Polans (western)"), who gave [Poland its name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_of_Poland "Names of Poland"). The process of establishing [statehood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statehood "Statehood") coincided with the conversion of a [pagan ruler of the Polans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mieszko_I "Mieszko I") to Christianity in 966 under the auspices of the [Roman Catholic Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church"). The [Kingdom of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland "Kingdom of Poland") emerged in 1025, and in 1569 cemented its long-standing [association with Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_union "Polish–Lithuanian union"), thus forming the [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth"). At the time, the Commonwealth was one of the [great powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_modern_great_powers "List of modern great powers") of Europe, with an [elective monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elective_monarchy_in_Poland "Elective monarchy in Poland") and a [uniquely liberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Liberty "Golden Liberty") political system, which adopted [Europe's first modern constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_3_May_1791 "Constitution of 3 May 1791") in 1791.

With the passing of the prosperous [Polish Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Golden_Age "Polish Golden Age"), the country was [partitioned by neighbouring states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland "Partitions of Poland") at the end of the 18th century. At the end of [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") in 1918, Poland regained [its independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Independence_Day_\(Poland\) "National Independence Day (Poland)") with the [founding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Poland_\(1795-1918\)#Recovery_of_statehood "History of Poland (1795-1918)") of the [Second Polish Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic"), which emerged [victorious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_\(1920\) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)") in [various conflicts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Poland#Second_Polish_Republic_\(1918%E2%80%931939\) "List of wars involving Poland") of the [interbellum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Poland_\(1918%E2%80%931939\) "History of Poland (1918–1939)") period. In September 1939, the [invasion of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland "Invasion of Poland") by [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") [and the](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland "Soviet invasion of Poland") [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") marked the beginning of [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), which resulted in [the Holocaust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Poland "The Holocaust in Poland") and millions of [Polish casualties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Poland_\(1939%E2%80%931945\) "History of Poland (1939–1945)") as well as [extensive border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Poland "Territorial evolution of Poland") and demographic changes. Forced into the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") in the global [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"), the [Polish People's Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic "Polish People's Republic") was a signatory of the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact"). Through the 1980 [emergence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_Agreement "Gdańsk Agreement") and contributions of the [Solidarity movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solidarity_\(Polish_trade_union\) "Solidarity (Polish trade union)"), which initiated the [fall of the Iron Curtain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_the_Iron_Curtain "Fall of the Iron Curtain"), the [communist government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_United_Workers%27_Party "Polish United Workers' Party") was [dissolved](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Poland_\(1945%E2%80%931989\) "History of Poland (1945–1989)") and Poland as the first of the [communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communism "Communism") countries re-established itself as a [liberal democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democracy "Liberal democracy") in 1989, and [held free elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_Polish_parliamentary_election "1989 Polish parliamentary election").

Poland is a [parliamentary republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_republic "Parliamentary republic") with its [bicameral legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameralism "Bicameralism") comprising the [Sejm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sejm "Sejm") and the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_of_Poland "Senate of Poland"). Considered a [middle power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_power "Middle power") and a [regional power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power "Regional power"), it is a [developed market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_market "Developed market") and [high-income economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy "World Bank high-income economy"). In terms of nominal GDP, it is the [20th largest economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)") in the world and the sixth in the European Union, and [fifth largest by PPP-adjusted GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(PPP\) "List of countries by GDP (PPP)") in the EU. Poland has a high standard of living, safety, and [economic freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_freedom "Economic freedom"), as well as free [university education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_in_Poland "Education in Poland") and [universal health care](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_care_in_Poland "Health care in Poland"). It has [17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Poland "List of World Heritage Sites in Poland") UNESCO [World Heritage Sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites "World Heritage Sites"), over 100 [Historic Monuments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Historic_Monuments_\(Poland\) "List of Historic Monuments (Poland)") and 23 [national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Parks_of_Poland "National Parks of Poland"). Poland is a founding member of the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"), and a member of the [Council of Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe"), [World Trade Organisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization "World Trade Organization"), [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD"), [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO"), and EU (including the [Schengen Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schengen_Area "Schengen Area")).

## Etymology

The native [Polish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language") name for Poland is *Polska*.[^20] It is believed that the name derives from the [Polans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polans_\(western\) "Polans (western)"), a [West Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Slavs "West Slavs") tribe who inhabited the [Warta River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warta_River "Warta River") basin of present-day [Greater Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland "Greater Poland") region (6th–8th century CE).[^21] The tribe's name stems from the [Proto-Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Slavic "Proto-Slavic") noun *pole*, meaning field, which itself originates from the [Proto-Indo-European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language "Proto-Indo-European language") word *\*pleh₂-* indicating flatland.[^22] The etymology alludes to the [topography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topography "Topography") of the region and the flat landscape of Greater Poland.[^23] [^24] During the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"), the [Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin "Latin") form *Polonia* was widely used throughout Europe.[^25]

The country's alternative archaic name is *[Lechia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lechia "Lechia")* and its root syllable remains in official use in several languages, notably [Hungarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_language "Hungarian language"), [Lithuanian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language"), and [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language").[^26] The [exonym](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exonym "Exonym") possibly derives from either [Lech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lech_and_Czech "Lech and Czech"), a legendary ruler of the [Lechites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lechites "Lechites"), or from the [Lendians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lendians "Lendians"), a West Slavic tribe that dwelt on the south-easternmost edge of [Lesser Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lesser_Poland "Lesser Poland").[^27] [^28] The origin of the tribe's name lies in the [Old Polish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Polish_language "Old Polish language") word *lęda* (plain).[^29] Initially, both names *Lechia* and *Polonia* were used interchangeably when referring to Poland by chroniclers during the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages").[^30]

## History

### Prehistory and protohistory

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Biskupin_brama_od_zewnatrz.jpg/250px-Biskupin_brama_od_zewnatrz.jpg)

A reconstruction of a Bronze Age Lusatian culture settlement in Biskupin, 8th century BC

The first [Stone Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stone_Age "Stone Age") archaic humans and *[Homo erectus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_erectus "Homo erectus")* species settled what was to become Poland approximately 500,000 years ago, though the ensuing hostile climate prevented early humans from founding more permanent encampments.[^31] The arrival of *[Homo sapiens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_sapiens "Homo sapiens")* and [anatomically modern humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_European_modern_humans "Early European modern humans") coincided with the climatic discontinuity at the end of the [Last Glacial Period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_Glacial_Period "Last Glacial Period") ([Northern Polish glaciation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weichselian_glaciation "Weichselian glaciation") 10,000 BC), when Poland became habitable.[^32] [Neolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic "Neolithic") excavations indicated broad-ranging development in that era; the earliest evidence of European cheesemaking (5500 BC) was discovered in Polish [Kuyavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuyavia "Kuyavia"),[^33] and the [Bronocice pot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronocice_pot "Bronocice pot") is incised with the earliest known depiction of what may be a wheeled vehicle (3400 BC).[^34]

The period spanning the [Bronze Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronze_Age "Bronze Age") and the [Early Iron Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Iron_Age "Early Iron Age") (1300 BC–500 BC) was marked by an increase in population density, establishment of [palisaded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palisade "Palisade") settlements ([gords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gord_\(archaeology\) "Gord (archaeology)")) and the expansion of [Lusatian culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusatian_culture "Lusatian culture").[^35] [^36] A significant archaeological find from [the protohistory of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_and_protohistory_of_Poland "Prehistory and protohistory of Poland") is a fortified settlement at [Biskupin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biskupin "Biskupin"), attributed to the Lusatian culture of the [Late Bronze Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age "Late Bronze Age") (mid-8th century BC).[^37]

Throughout [antiquity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_antiquity "Classical antiquity") (400 BC–500 AD), many distinct ancient populations inhabited the territory of present-day Poland, notably [Celtic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celts "Celts"), [Scythian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scythia "Scythia"), [Germanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanic_peoples "Germanic peoples"), [Sarmatian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarmatians "Sarmatians"), [Baltic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balts "Balts") and [Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Slavs "Early Slavs") tribes.[^38] Furthermore, archaeological findings confirmed the presence of [Roman Legions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Legions "Roman Legions") sent to protect the [amber trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amber_Road "Amber Road").[^39] The [Polish tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_tribes "Polish tribes") emerged following the [second wave of the Migration Period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Migration_Period#Second_wave "Migration Period") around the 6th century AD;[^25] they were [Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavs "Slavs") and may have included assimilated remnants of peoples that earlier dwelled in the area.[^40] [^41] Beginning in the early 10th century, the [Polans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polans_\(western\) "Polans (western)") would come to dominate other [Lechitic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lechites "Lechites") tribes in the region, initially forming a tribal federation and later a centralised monarchical state.[^42]

### Kingdom of Poland

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Poland960.png/250px-Poland960.png)

Poland under the rule of Duke Mieszko I, whose acceptance of Christianity under the auspices of the Roman Church and the Baptism of Poland marked the beginning of statehood in 966. His son, Bolesław I the Brave, was crowned king in 1025

Poland began to form into a recognisable unitary and territorial entity around the middle of the 10th century under the [Piast dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piast_dynasty "Piast dynasty").[^43] In 966, the ruler of the Polans, [Mieszko I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mieszko_I_of_Poland "Mieszko I of Poland"), accepted [Western Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Christianity "Western Christianity") under the auspices of the [Roman Catholic Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church "Roman Catholic Church") which was tantamount to the adoption of [Christianity by Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianization_of_Poland "Christianization of Poland").[^44] In 968, a missionary [bishopric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bishopric "Bishopric") was established in [Poznań](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pozna%C5%84 "Poznań"). An [incipit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incipit "Incipit") titled [Dagome iudex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dagome_iudex "Dagome iudex") first defined Poland's geographical boundaries with its capital in [Gniezno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gniezno "Gniezno") and affirmed that its monarchy was under the protection of the [Apostolic See](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apostolic_See "Apostolic See").[^45] The country's early origins were described by [Gallus Anonymus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gallus_Anonymus "Gallus Anonymus") in *[Gesta principum Polonorum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gesta_principum_Polonorum "Gesta principum Polonorum")*, the oldest Polish chronicle.[^46] An important national event of the period was the [martyrdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martyrdom "Martyrdom") of [Saint Adalbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adalbert_of_Prague "Adalbert of Prague"), who was killed by [Prussian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Prussians "Old Prussians") pagans in 997 and whose remains were reputedly bought back for their weight in gold by Mieszko's successor, [Bolesław I the Brave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_I_the_Brave "Bolesław I the Brave").[^45]

In 1000, at the [Congress of Gniezno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Gniezno "Congress of Gniezno"), Bolesław I the Brave obtained the right of [investiture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Investiture "Investiture") from [Otto III, Holy Roman Emperor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Otto III, Holy Roman Emperor"), who assented to the creation archdioceses in Gniezno [^45] and three new dioceses on Polish lands in [Kraków](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków"), [Kołobrzeg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ko%C5%82obrzeg "Kołobrzeg"), and [Wrocław](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw "Wrocław").[^47] Also, Otto bestowed upon Bolesław royal [regalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regalia "Regalia") and a replica of the [Holy Lance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Lance "Holy Lance"), which were later used at his coronation as the first [King of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs "List of Polish monarchs") c. 1025, when Bolesław received permission for his coronation from [Pope John XIX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_John_XIX "Pope John XIX").[^48] [^49] Bolesław also expanded the realm considerably by seizing parts of German [Lusatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lusatia "Lusatia"), Czech [Moravia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moravia "Moravia"), [Upper Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Hungary "Upper Hungary"), and southwestern regions of the [Kievan Rus'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27 "Kievan Rus'").[^50]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Casimir_the_Great_by_Leopold_L%C3%B6ffler.PNG/250px-Casimir_the_Great_by_Leopold_L%C3%B6ffler.PNG)

Casimir III the Great is the only Polish king to receive the title of Great. He built extensively during his reign, and reformed the Polish army along with the country's legal code, 1333–1370.

The transition from [paganism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavic_paganism "Slavic paganism") in Poland was not instantaneous and resulted in the [pagan reaction of the 1030s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pagan_reaction_in_Poland "Pagan reaction in Poland").[^51] In 1031, [Mieszko II Lambert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mieszko_II_Lambert "Mieszko II Lambert") lost the title of king and fled amidst the violence.[^52] The unrest led to the transfer of the capital to Kraków in 1038 by [Casimir I the Restorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casimir_I_the_Restorer "Casimir I the Restorer").[^53] In 1076, [Bolesław II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_II_the_Generous "Bolesław II the Generous") re-instituted the office of king, but was banished in 1079 for murdering his opponent, [Bishop Stanislaus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanislaus_of_Szczepan%C3%B3w "Stanislaus of Szczepanów").[^54] In 1138, the country [fragmented](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testament_of_Boles%C5%82aw_III_Wrymouth "Testament of Bolesław III Wrymouth") into five principalities when [Bolesław III Wrymouth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_III_Wrymouth "Bolesław III Wrymouth") divided his lands among his sons.[^27] These were [Lesser Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lesser_Poland "Lesser Poland"), Greater Poland, [Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silesia "Silesia"), [Masovia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masovia "Masovia"), and [Sandomierz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandomierz "Sandomierz"), with intermittent hold over [Pomerania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pomerania "Pomerania").[^55] In 1226, [Konrad I of Masovia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konrad_I_of_Masovia "Konrad I of Masovia") invited the [Teutonic Knights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teutonic_Knights "Teutonic Knights") to aid in combating the [Baltic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balts "Balts") Prussians; a decision that later led to centuries of warfare with the Knights.[^56]

In the first half of the 13th century, [Henry I the Bearded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_I_the_Bearded "Henry I the Bearded") and [Henry II the Pious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_II_the_Pious "Henry II the Pious") aimed to unite the fragmented dukedoms, but the [Mongol invasion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Mongol_invasion_of_Poland "First Mongol invasion of Poland") and the death of Henry II in [battle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Legnica "Battle of Legnica") hindered the unification.[^57] [^58] As a result of the devastation which followed, depopulation and the demand for craft labour spurred a migration of [German and Flemish settlers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Germans_in_Poland "History of Germans in Poland") into Poland, which was encouraged by the Polish dukes.[^59] In 1264, the [Statute of Kalisz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statute_of_Kalisz "Statute of Kalisz") introduced unprecedented autonomy for the [Polish Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland "History of the Jews in Poland"), who came to Poland fleeing persecution elsewhere in Europe.[^60]

In 1320, [Władysław I the Short](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_I_the_Elbow-high "Władysław I the Elbow-high") became the first king of [a reunified Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_\(1025%E2%80%931385\) "Kingdom of Poland (1025–1385)") since [Przemysł II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Przemys%C5%82_II "Przemysł II") in 1296,[^61] and the first to be crowned at [Wawel Cathedral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral "Wawel Cathedral") in Kraków.[^62] Beginning in 1333, the reign of [Casimir III the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casimir_III_the_Great "Casimir III the Great") was marked by developments in [castle infrastructure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trail_of_the_Eagle%27s_Nests "Trail of the Eagle's Nests"), army, judiciary and [diplomacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Krak%C3%B3w "Congress of Kraków").[^63] [^64] Under his authority, Poland transformed into a major European power; he instituted Polish rule over [Ruthenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ruthenia "Kingdom of Ruthenia") in 1340 and imposed quarantine that prevented the spread of [Black Death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death "Black Death").[^65] [^66] In 1364, Casimir inaugurated the [University of Kraków](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jagiellonian_University "Jagiellonian University"), one of the oldest institutions of higher learning in Europe.[^67] Upon his death in 1370, the Piast dynasty came to an end.[^68] He was succeeded by his closest male relative, [Louis of Anjou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_I_of_Hungary "Louis I of Hungary"), who ruled Poland, [Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary "Kingdom of Hungary"), and [Croatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatia_in_personal_union_with_Hungary "Croatia in personal union with Hungary") in a [personal union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_union "Personal union").[^69] Louis' younger daughter [Jadwiga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland "Jadwiga of Poland") became Poland's first female monarch in [1384](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1384 "1384").[^69]

### The Golden Age

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Battle_of_Tannenberg.jpg/250px-Battle_of_Tannenberg.jpg)

The Battle of Grunwald was fought against the German Order of Teutonic Knights, and resulted in a decisive victory for the Kingdom of Poland, 15 July 1410.

In 1386, Jadwiga of Poland entered a marriage of convenience with [Władysław II Jagiełło](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o "Władysław II Jagiełło"), the [Grand Duke of Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Lithuania "Grand Duke of Lithuania"), thus forming the [Jagiellonian dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jagiellonian_dynasty "Jagiellonian dynasty") and the [Polish–Lithuanian union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_union "Polish–Lithuanian union") which spanned the late [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages") and early [Modern Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_history "Modern history").[^70] The partnership between Poles and Lithuanians brought the vast multi-ethnic [Lithuanian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania") territories into Poland's sphere of influence and proved beneficial for its inhabitants, who coexisted in one of the largest European [political entities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_union "Personal union") of the time.[^71]

In the Baltic Sea region, the struggle of Poland and Lithuania with the [Teutonic Knights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teutonic_Knights "Teutonic Knights") continued and culminated at the [Battle of Grunwald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald "Battle of Grunwald") in [1410](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1410 "1410"), where a combined Polish–Lithuanian army inflicted a decisive victory against them.[^72] In 1466, after the [Thirteen Years' War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteen_Years%27_War_\(1454%E2%80%9366\) "Thirteen Years' War (1454–66)"), king [Casimir IV Jagiellon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon "Casimir IV Jagiellon") gave royal consent to the [Peace of Thorn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Peace_of_Thorn_\(1466\) "Second Peace of Thorn (1466)"), which created the future [Duchy of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia "Duchy of Prussia") under Polish suzerainty and forced the Prussian rulers to pay [tributes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homage_\(feudal\) "Homage (feudal)").[^27] The Jagiellonian dynasty also established dynastic control over the kingdoms of [Bohemia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia "Kingdom of Bohemia") ([1471](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1471 "1471") onwards) and Hungary.[^73] In the south, Poland confronted the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") (at the [Varna Crusade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Varna "Battle of Varna")) and the [Crimean Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Khanate "Crimean Khanate"), and in the east helped Lithuania to combat [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow "Grand Duchy of Moscow").[^27]

Poland was developing as a [feudal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feudalism "Feudalism") state, with a predominantly agricultural economy and an increasingly powerful [landed nobility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landed_nobility "Landed nobility") that confined the population to private manorial farmstead known as [*folwarks*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folwark "Folwark").[^74] In 1493, [John I Albert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_I_Albert "John I Albert") sanctioned the creation of a [bicameral parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameral_parliament "Bicameral parliament") (the Sejm) composed of a lower house, the chamber of deputies, and an upper house, the chamber of senators.[^75] The *[Nihil novi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nihil_novi "Nihil novi")* act adopted by the Polish [General Sejm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Sejm "General Sejm") in 1505, transferred most of the [legislative power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legislature "Legislature") from the monarch to the parliament, an event which marked the beginning of the period known as [Golden Liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Liberty "Golden Liberty"), when the state was ruled by the seemingly free and equal [Polish nobles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Szlachta "Szlachta").[^76]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Wawel_%284%29.jpg/330px-Wawel_%284%29.jpg)

Wawel Castle in Kraków, seat of Polish kings from 1038 until the capital was moved to Warsaw in 1596

The 16th century saw [Protestant Reformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestant_Reformation "Protestant Reformation") movements making deep inroads into Polish Christianity, which resulted in the establishment of policies promoting religious tolerance, unique in Europe at that time.[^77] This tolerance allowed the country to avoid the religious turmoil and [wars of religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_wars_of_religion "European wars of religion") that beset Europe.[^77] In Poland, [Nontrinitarian Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nontrinitarianism "Nontrinitarianism") became the doctrine of the so-called [Polish Brethren](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Brethren "Polish Brethren"), who separated from their [Calvinist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calvinism "Calvinism") denomination and became the co-founders of global [Unitarianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitarianism "Unitarianism").[^78]

The European [Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance "Renaissance") evoked under [Sigismund I the Old](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old "Sigismund I the Old") and [Sigismund II Augustus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus "Sigismund II Augustus") a sense of urgency in the need to promote a [cultural awakening](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland "Renaissance in Poland"). During the [Polish Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Golden_Age "Polish Golden Age"), the nation's economy and culture flourished. The Italian-born [Bona Sforza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bona_Sforza "Bona Sforza"), daughter of the [Duke of Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gian_Galeazzo_Sforza "Gian Galeazzo Sforza") and queen consort to Sigismund I, made considerable contributions to [architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture_of_Poland "Architecture of Poland"), [cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_cuisine "Polish cuisine"), language and court customs at [Wawel Castle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wawel_Castle "Wawel Castle").[^27]

### Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth_in_1619.PNG/330px-Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth_in_1619.PNG)

The Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth at its greatest extent in 1619. At that time it was the largest country in Europe

The [Union of Lublin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_of_Lublin "Union of Lublin") of 1569 established the [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth"), a unified federal state with an [elective monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elective_monarchy "Elective monarchy") that was largely governed by the nobility.[^79] The latter coincided with a period of prosperity. The Polish-dominated union thereafter became a leading power and a major cultural entity, exercising political control over parts of Central, [Eastern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Europe "Eastern Europe"), [Southeastern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_Europe "Southeastern Europe") and Northern Europe. The Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth occupied approximately 1 million km <sup>2</sup> (390,000 sq mi) [at its peak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truce_of_Deulino "Truce of Deulino") and was the largest state in Europe.[^80] [^81] Simultaneously, Poland imposed [Polonisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polonisation "Polonisation") policies in newly acquired territories which were met with resistance from ethnic and religious minorities.[^79]

In [1573](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1573 "1573"), [Henry de Valois of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_III_of_France "Henry III of France"), the first elected king, approbated the [Henrician Articles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henrician_Articles "Henrician Articles") which obliged future monarchs to respect the rights of nobles.[^82] When he left Poland to become [King of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_French_monarchs "List of French monarchs"), his successor, [Stephen Báthory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_B%C3%A1thory "Stephen Báthory"), led a successful [campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Livonian_campaign_of_Stephen_B%C3%A1thory "Livonian campaign of Stephen Báthory") in the [Livonian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Livonian_War "Livonian War"), granting Poland more [lands across the eastern shores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Livonia "Livonia") of the Baltic Sea.[^83] State affairs were then headed by [Jan Zamoyski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Zamoyski "Jan Zamoyski"), the [Crown Chancellor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chancellor_\(Poland\) "Chancellor (Poland)").[^84] Stephen's successor, [Sigismund III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa "Sigismund III Vasa"), defeated a rival [Habsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Habsburg "House of Habsburg") electoral candidate, [Archduke Maximilian III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximilian_III,_Archduke_of_Austria "Maximilian III, Archduke of Austria"), in the [War of the Polish Succession (1587–1588)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession_\(1587%E2%80%931588\) "War of the Polish Succession (1587–1588)"). In [1592](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1592 "1592"), Sigismund succeeded his father [John Vasa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_III_of_Sweden "John III of Sweden"), in [Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sweden "Kingdom of Sweden").[^85] The [Polish-Swedish union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish-Swedish_union "Polish-Swedish union") endured until 1599, when he was [deposed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_against_Sigismund "War against Sigismund") by the Swedes.[^86]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Daniel_Schultz%2C_Portret_Jana_III_Sobieskiego%2C_kr%C3%B3la_Polski.jpg/250px-Daniel_Schultz%2C_Portret_Jana_III_Sobieskiego%2C_kr%C3%B3la_Polski.jpg)

King John III Sobieski defeated the Ottoman Turks at the Battle of Vienna on 12 September 1683.

In 1609, Sigismund [invaded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Muscovite_War_\(1605%E2%80%931618\) "Polish–Muscovite War (1605–1618)") [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia "Tsardom of Russia") which was engulfed in a [civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_of_Troubles "Time of Troubles"),[^27] and a year later the Polish [winged hussar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_hussars "Polish hussars") units under [Stanisław Żółkiewski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_%C5%BB%C3%B3%C5%82kiewski "Stanisław Żółkiewski") [occupied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_occupation_of_Moscow "Polish–Lithuanian occupation of Moscow") Moscow for two years after defeating the Russians at [Klushino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Klushino "Battle of Klushino").[^27] Sigismund also countered the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") in the southeast; at [Khotyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Khotyn_\(1621\) "Battle of Khotyn (1621)") in [1621](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1621 "1621") [Jan Karol Chodkiewicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Karol_Chodkiewicz "Jan Karol Chodkiewicz") achieved a decisive victory against the Turks, which ushered the downfall of Sultan [Osman II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osman_II "Osman II").[^87] [^88] Sigismund's long reign in Poland coincided with the [Silver Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa#Legacy "Sigismund III Vasa").[^89] The liberal [Władysław IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_IV_Vasa "Władysław IV Vasa") effectively defended Poland's territorial possessions but after his death the vast Commonwealth began declining from internal disorder and constant warfare.[^90] [^91]

In 1648, the Polish hegemony over Ukraine sparked the [Khmelnytsky Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khmelnytsky_Uprising "Khmelnytsky Uprising"),[^92] followed by the decimating [Swedish Deluge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deluge_\(history\) "Deluge (history)") during the [Second Northern War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Northern_War "Second Northern War"),[^93] and Prussia's [independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Bromberg "Treaty of Bromberg") in 1657.[^93] In 1683, [John III Sobieski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_III_Sobieski "John III Sobieski") re-established military prowess when he halted the advance of an [Ottoman Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Army_\(15th-19th_centuries\) "Ottoman Army (15th-19th centuries)") into Europe at the [Battle of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna "Battle of Vienna").[^94] The [Saxon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Wettin "House of Wettin") era, under [Augustus II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_II_the_Strong "Augustus II the Strong") and [Augustus III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland "Augustus III of Poland"), saw neighbouring powers grow in strength at the expense of Poland. Both Saxon kings faced opposition from [Stanisław Leszczyński](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Leszczy%C5%84ski "Stanisław Leszczyński") during the [Great Northern War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Northern_War "Great Northern War") (1700) and the [War of the Polish Succession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession "War of the Polish Succession") (1733).[^95]

### Partitions

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Stanis%C5%82aw_II_August_Poniatowski_in_coronation_clothes.PNG/250px-Stanis%C5%82aw_II_August_Poniatowski_in_coronation_clothes.PNG)

Stanisław II Augustus, the last King of Poland, reigned from 1764 until his abdication on 25 November 1795.

The [royal election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_elections_in_Poland "Royal elections in Poland") of 1764 resulted in the elevation of [Stanisław II Augustus Poniatowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_August_Poniatowski "Stanisław August Poniatowski") to the monarchy.[^96] His candidacy was extensively funded by his sponsor and former lover, Empress [Catherine II of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_II_of_Russia "Catherine II of Russia").[^97] The new king maneuvered between his desire to implement necessary modernising reforms, and the necessity to remain at peace with surrounding states.[^98] His ideals led to the formation of the 1768 [Bar Confederation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_Confederation "Bar Confederation"), a rebellion directed against the Poniatowski and all external influence, which ineptly aimed to preserve Poland's sovereignty and privileges held by the nobility.[^99] The failed attempts at government restructuring as well as the domestic turmoil provoked its neighbours to invade.[^100]

In 1772, the [First Partition of the Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Partition_of_Poland "First Partition of Poland") by Prussia, Russia, and Austria took place, an act which the [Partition Sejm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_Sejm "Partition Sejm"), under considerable duress, eventually ratified as a [fait accompli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_French_words_and_phrases_used_by_English_speakers#F "List of French words and phrases used by English speakers").[^101] Disregarding the territorial losses, in 1773 a plan of critical reforms was established, in which the [Commission of National Education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commission_of_National_Education "Commission of National Education"), the first government education authority in Europe, was inaugurated.[^102] Corporal punishment of schoolchildren was officially prohibited in 1783. Poniatowski was the head figure of the [Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Enlightenment "Polish Enlightenment"), encouraged the development of industries, and embraced republican [neoclassicism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture "Neoclassical architecture").[^103] For his contributions to the arts and sciences, he was awarded a [Fellowship of the Royal Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fellowship_of_the_Royal_Society "Fellowship of the Royal Society").[^104]

In 1791, the [Great Sejm parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Sejm "Great Sejm") adopted the [3 May Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_May_3,_1791 "Constitution of May 3, 1791"), the first set of supreme national laws, and introduced a [constitutional monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy "Constitutional monarchy").[^105] The [Targowica Confederation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Targowica_Confederation "Targowica Confederation"), an organisation of nobles and deputies opposing the act, appealed to Catherine and caused the [1792 Polish–Russian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Russian_War_of_1792 "Polish–Russian War of 1792").[^106] Fearing the reemergence of Polish hegemony, Russia and Prussia arranged and, in 1793, executed the [Second Partition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Partition_of_Poland "Second Partition of Poland"), which left the country deprived of territory and incapable of independent existence. On 24 October 1795, the Commonwealth was [partitioned for the third time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Partition_of_Poland "Third Partition of Poland") and ceased to exist as a territorial entity.[^107] [^108] Stanisław Augustus, the last King of Poland, abdicated the throne on 25 November 1795.[^109]

### Era of insurrections

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Rzeczpospolita_Rozbiory_3.png/330px-Rzeczpospolita_Rozbiory_3.png)

The partitions of Poland, carried out by the Kingdom of Prussia ( blue ), the Russian Empire brown ), and the Austrian Habsburg Monarchy green ) in 1772, 1793 and 1795

The Polish people [rose several times against the partitioners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Poland "List of wars involving Poland") and occupying armies. An unsuccessful attempt at defending Poland's sovereignty took place in the 1794 [Kościuszko Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Uprising "Kościuszko Uprising"), where a popular and distinguished general [Tadeusz Kościuszko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko "Tadeusz Kościuszko"), who had several years earlier served under [George Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington "George Washington") in the [American Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War"), led Polish insurgents.[^110] Despite the victory at the [Battle of Racławice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Rac%C5%82awice "Battle of Racławice"), his ultimate defeat ended Poland's independent existence [for 123 years](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Partition_of_Poland "Third Partition of Poland").[^111]

In 1806, an [insurrection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland_uprising_\(1806\) "Greater Poland uprising (1806)") organised by [Jan Henryk Dąbrowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Henryk_D%C4%85browski "Jan Henryk Dąbrowski") liberated western Poland ahead of [Napoleon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France "Napoleon I of France") 's advance into Prussia during the [War of the Fourth Coalition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Fourth_Coalition "War of the Fourth Coalition"). In accordance with the 1807 [Treaty of Tilsit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Tilsit "Treaty of Tilsit"), Napoleon proclaimed the [Duchy of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw "Duchy of Warsaw"), a [client state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Client_state "Client state") ruled by his ally [Frederick Augustus I of Saxony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_Augustus_I_of_Saxony "Frederick Augustus I of Saxony"). The Poles actively aided French troops in the [Napoleonic Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars "Napoleonic Wars"), particularly those under [Józef Poniatowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Poniatowski "Józef Poniatowski") who became [Marshal of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshal_of_the_Empire "Marshal of the Empire") shortly before his death at [Leipzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig "Battle of Leipzig") in 1813.[^112] In the aftermath of Napoleon's exile, the Duchy of Warsaw was abolished at the [Congress of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna "Congress of Vienna") in 1815 and its territory was divided into Russian [Congress Kingdom of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_Kingdom_of_Poland "Congress Kingdom of Poland"), the Prussian [Grand Duchy of Posen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Posen "Grand Duchy of Posen"), and [Austrian Galicia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Poland "Austrian Poland") with the [Free City of Kraków](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_City_of_Krak%C3%B3w "Free City of Kraków").[^113]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Karl_G_Schweikart_-_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_%28%C3%96aL%29.jpg/250px-Karl_G_Schweikart_-_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_%28%C3%96aL%29.jpg) ![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Karl_G_Schweikart_-_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_%28%C3%96aL%29.jpg/250px-Karl_G_Schweikart_-_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_%28%C3%96aL%29.jpg)

[Tadeusz Kościuszko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko "Tadeusz Kościuszko") was a veteran and hero of both the [Polish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Russian_War_of_1792 "Polish–Russian War of 1792") and [American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War") wars of independence.[^110]

In 1830, [non-commissioned officers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer "Non-commissioned officer") at Warsaw's [Officer Cadet School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corps_of_Cadets_\(Warsaw\) "Corps of Cadets (Warsaw)") rebelled in what was the [November Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/November_Uprising "November Uprising").[^114] After its collapse, Congress Poland lost its [constitutional autonomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Congress_Poland "Constitution of Congress Poland"), [army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_Congress_Poland "Army of Congress Poland") and legislative assembly.[^115] During the [European Spring of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spring_of_Nations "Spring of Nations"), Poles took up arms in the [Greater Poland Uprising of 1848](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Poland_Uprising_\(1848\) "Greater Poland Uprising (1848)") to resist [Germanisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanisation "Germanisation"), but its failure saw the duchy's status reduced to a mere [province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_Posen "Province of Posen"); and subsequent integration into the [German Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Empire "German Empire") in 1871.[^116] In Russia, the fall of the [January Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_Uprising "January Uprising") (1863–1864) prompted severe [political, social and cultural reprisals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_Uprising#The_decades_of_reprisals "January Uprising"), followed by deportations and [pogroms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogroms "Pogroms") of the Polish-Jewish population. Towards the end of the 19th century, Congress Poland became heavily industrialised; its primary exports being coal, [zinc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinc "Zinc"), iron and textiles.[^117] [^118]

### Second Polish Republic

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski_%28-1930%29.jpg/250px-J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski_%28-1930%29.jpg)

Chief of State Marshal Józef Piłsudski was a hero of the Polish independence campaign and the nation's premiere statesman from 1918 until his death on 12 May 1935.

In the aftermath of [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), the [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") agreed on the reconstitution of Poland, confirmed through the [Treaty of Versailles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles "Treaty of Versailles") of June 1919.[^119] A total of 2 million Poles served in the armies of the German Empire, Austria-Hungary, and the Russian Empire, and over 450,000 died.[^120] Following the [armistice with Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_with_Germany_\(Compi%C3%A8gne\) "Armistice with Germany (Compiègne)") in November 1918, Poland regained its independence as the [Second Polish Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic").[^121]

The Second Polish Republic reaffirmed its sovereignty after [a series of military conflicts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Poland "List of wars involving Poland"), most notably the [Polish–Soviet War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish–Soviet War"), when Poland inflicted a crushing defeat on the [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") at the [Battle of Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_\(1920\) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)").[^122]

The inter-war period heralded a new era of Polish politics. Whilst Polish political activists had faced heavy censorship in the decades up until [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), a new political tradition was established in the country. Many exiled Polish activists, such as [Ignacy Jan Paderewski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ignacy_Jan_Paderewski "Ignacy Jan Paderewski"), who would later become prime minister, returned home. A significant number of them then went on to take key positions in the newly formed political and governmental structures. Tragedy struck in 1922 when [Gabriel Narutowicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel_Narutowicz "Gabriel Narutowicz"), inaugural holder of the presidency, was assassinated at the [Zachęta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zach%C4%99ta "Zachęta") Gallery in Warsaw by a painter and right-wing nationalist [Eligiusz Niewiadomski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eligiusz_Niewiadomski "Eligiusz Niewiadomski").[^123]

In 1926, the [May Coup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_Coup_\(Poland\) "May Coup (Poland)"), led by the hero of the Polish independence campaign Marshal [Józef Piłsudski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "Józef Piłsudski"), turned rule of the Second Polish Republic over to the nonpartisan [Sanacja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanacja "Sanacja") (*Healing*) movement to prevent radical political organisations on both the left and the right from destabilising the country.[^124] By the late 1930s, due to increased threats posed by political extremism inside the country, the Polish government became increasingly heavy-handed, banning a number of radical organisations, including communist and ultra-nationalist political parties, which threatened the stability of the country.[^125]

### World War II

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/7TP_Polish_Tank.png/250px-7TP_Polish_Tank.png)

Polish Army 7TP tanks on military manoeuvres shortly before the invasion of Poland in 1939

World War II began with the [Nazi German](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_German "Nazi German") [invasion of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland "Invasion of Poland") on 1 September 1939, followed by the [Soviet invasion of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland "Soviet invasion of Poland") on 17 September. As agreed in the [Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact"), Poland was split into two zones, [one occupied by Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_areas_annexed_by_Nazi_Germany "Polish areas annexed by Nazi Germany"), the other by [the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union "Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union"). The [wartime resistance movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_resistance_movement_in_World_War_II "Polish resistance movement in World War II"), and the [Armia Krajowa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armia_Krajowa "Armia Krajowa") (*Home Army*), fought against the occupation. It was one of the three largest resistance movements of the entire war, and encompassed a range of clandestine activities, which functioned as an [underground state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Underground_State "Polish Underground State") complete with [degree-awarding universities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_in_Poland_during_World_War_II "Education in Poland during World War II") and [a court system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Underground_court "Underground court").[^126] The resistance was loyal to the [Polish Government in Exile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Government_in_Exile "Polish Government in Exile") and generally resented the idea of a post-war communist Poland; for this reason, in the summer of 1944 it initiated [Operation Tempest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Tempest "Operation Tempest"), of which the [Warsaw Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising "Warsaw Uprising") that began on 1 August 1944 is the best-known operation.[^127] [^128]

Poland made the fourth-largest troop contribution in Europe,[^129] [^130] [^131] and its troops served both the exiled government in the [west](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces_in_the_West "Polish Armed Forces in the West") and Soviet leadership in the [east](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces_in_the_East "Polish Armed Forces in the East"). Polish troops played an important role in the [Normandy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Overlord "Operation Overlord"), [Italian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Campaign_\(World_War_II\) "Italian Campaign (World War II)"), [North African Campaigns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_African_Campaign "North African Campaign") and [Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pheasant "Operation Pheasant") and are particularly remembered for the [Battle of Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Britain "Battle of Britain") and [Battle of Monte Cassino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Cassino "Battle of Monte Cassino").[^132] [^133] Polish intelligence operatives proved extremely valuable to the Allies, providing much of the intelligence from Europe and beyond,[^134] [Polish code breakers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Cipher_Bureau "Polish Cipher Bureau") were responsible for [cracking the Enigma cipher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptanalysis_of_the_Enigma "Cryptanalysis of the Enigma") and Polish scientists participating in the [Manhattan Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project") were co-creators of the American [atomic bomb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bomb "Atomic bomb"). In the east, the Soviet-backed [Polish 1st Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Polish_Army_\(1944%E2%80%931945\) "First Polish Army (1944–1945)") distinguished itself in the battles for [Warsaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising "Warsaw Uprising") and [Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin "Battle of Berlin").[^127]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG/250px-WW2-Holocaust-Poland.PNG)

Map of the Holocaust in German-occupied Poland with marked deportation routes, major ghettos and Nazi extermination camps. The border in 1941 between Nazi Germany and the Soviet Union is marked in red.

The actions undertaken by both occupiers within Polish territory were [genocidal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide"). In 1939–1941, the Soviets deported hundreds of thousands of Poles and the Soviet [NKVD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NKVD "NKVD") executed thousands of Polish [prisoners of war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoners_of_war "Prisoners of war") ahead of [Operation Barbarossa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa"), notably in the [Katyn massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katyn_massacre "Katyn massacre").[^135] Around 150,000 Polish civilians were killed by Soviets during the Soviet Union's occupation of eastern Poland ([Kresy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kresy "Kresy")). Similarly, German planners had in November 1939 called for "the complete destruction of all Poles" and their fate as outlined in the *[Generalplan Ost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generalplan_Ost "Generalplan Ost")*;[^136] six German [extermination camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extermination_camp "Extermination camp") were established in occupied Poland, including [Treblinka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp "Treblinka extermination camp"), [Majdanek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majdanek_concentration_camp "Majdanek concentration camp") and [Auschwitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp "Auschwitz concentration camp"). The Germans [transported millions of Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_train "Holocaust train") from across occupied Europe to be murdered in those camps.[^137] [^138] Altogether, 3 million Polish Jews [^139] [^140] – approximately 90% of Poland's pre-war Jewry – and between 1.8 and 2.8 million ethnic Poles [^141] [^142] [^143] were killed, including up to 100,000 members of the Polish [intelligentsia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligentsia "Intelligentsia"). The [Romani people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romani_people "Romani people") were also exterminated.[^144] During the [Warsaw Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising "Warsaw Uprising") alone, over 150,000 Polish civilians were killed, most were murdered by the Germans during the [Wola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wola_massacre "Wola massacre") and [Ochota](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ochota_massacre "Ochota massacre") massacres.[^145] [^146] At least 100,000 Poles were also murdered by the [Ukrainian Insurgent Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army "Ukrainian Insurgent Army") (UPA) between 1943 and 1944 in what became known as the [Wołyń Massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massacres_of_Poles_in_Volhynia_and_Eastern_Galicia "Massacres of Poles in Volhynia and Eastern Galicia").[^147] [^148]

[Of all the countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties "World War II casualties") in the war, Poland lost the highest percentage of its citizens: around 6 million perished – more than one-sixth of Poland's pre-war population – [half of them](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust_in_Poland "Holocaust in Poland") Polish Jews.[^149] [^150] [^151] About 90% of deaths were non-military in nature.[^152] In 1945, Poland's borders [were shifted westwards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland_immediately_after_World_War_II "Territorial changes of Poland immediately after World War II"). The shift forced the migration of [millions of people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_evacuation_and_expulsion "World War II evacuation and expulsion").[^153] [^154] [^155] Over two million Polish inhabitants of [Kresy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kresy "Kresy") [were expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_population_transfers_\(1944%E2%80%931946\) "Polish population transfers (1944–1946)") along the [Curzon Line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curzon_Line "Curzon Line") by [Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin").[^156] Up to eight million [Germans were expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_from_Poland_during_and_after_World_War_II "Flight and expulsion of Germans from Poland during and after World War II") by Poland from the [territories it acquired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Former_eastern_territories_of_Germany "Former eastern territories of Germany").[^157] The western border became the [Oder-Neisse line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oder-Neisse_line "Oder-Neisse line"). As a result, Poland's territory was reduced by 20%, or 77,500 square kilometres (29,900 sq mi).

### Post-war communism

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg/250px-Solidarity_poster_1989.jpg)

At High Noon, 4 June 1989 —political poster featuring Gary Cooper to encourage votes for the Solidarity party in the 1989 elections

At the insistence of [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), the [Yalta Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference") sanctioned the formation of a new provisional pro-Communist coalition government in Moscow, which ignored the [Polish government-in-exile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile "Polish government-in-exile") based in London. This action angered many Poles who considered it a [betrayal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_betrayal "Yalta betrayal") by the Allies.[^158] In 1944, Stalin had made guarantees to [Churchill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") and [Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt") that he would maintain Poland's sovereignty and allow democratic elections to take place. However, upon achieving victory in 1945, the elections organised by the occupying Soviet authorities were falsified and were used to provide a veneer of legitimacy for Soviet hegemony over Polish affairs.[^159] [^160] [^161] The Soviet Union instituted a new [communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_state "Communist state") government in Poland, analogous to much of the rest of the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc"). [As elsewhere in Communist Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Communism_in_the_Communist_Bloc "Anti-Communism in the Communist Bloc"), the Soviet influence over Poland was met with [armed resistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cursed_soldiers "Cursed soldiers") from the outset which continued into the 1950s.[^162]

Despite widespread objections, the new Polish government accepted the Soviet annexation of the pre-war eastern regions of Poland [^163] (in particular the cities of [Wilno](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilno "Wilno") and [Lwów](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w "Lwów")) and agreed to the permanent garrisoning of [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") units on Poland's territory. Military alignment within the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact") throughout the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War") came about as a direct result of this change in Poland's political culture. In the European scene, it came to characterise the full-fledged integration of Poland into the brotherhood of communist nations.[^164]

The new communist government took control with the adoption of the [Small Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Constitution_of_1947 "Small Constitution of 1947") on 19 February 1947. The [Polish People's Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic "Polish People's Republic") (*Polska Rzeczpospolita Ludowa*) [was officially proclaimed in 1952](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_Poland "Constitution of the People's Republic of Poland").[^165] [^166] In 1956, after the death of [Bolesław Bierut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_Bierut "Bolesław Bierut"), the régime of [Władysław Gomułka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Gomu%C5%82ka "Władysław Gomułka") became temporarily more liberal, freeing many people from prison and expanding some personal freedoms. [Collectivisation in the Polish People's Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Polish_People%27s_Republic "Collectivization in the Polish People's Republic") failed. A similar situation repeated itself in the 1970s under [Edward Gierek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Gierek "Edward Gierek"), but most of the time persecution of [anti-communist opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communist_resistance_in_Poland_\(1944%E2%80%931989\) "Anti-communist resistance in Poland (1944–1989)") groups persisted. Despite this, Poland was at the time considered to be one of the least oppressive states of the Eastern Bloc.[^167]

Labour turmoil in 1980 led to the formation of the independent trade union " [Solidarity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solidarity_\(Polish_trade_union\) "Solidarity (Polish trade union)") " (" *Solidarność* "), which over time became a political force.[^168] Despite persecution and imposition of [martial law in 1981](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law_in_Poland "Martial law in Poland") by General [Wojciech Jaruzelski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wojciech_Jaruzelski "Wojciech Jaruzelski"), it eroded the dominance of the [Polish United Workers' Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_United_Workers%27_Party "Polish United Workers' Party") and by 1989 had triumphed in Poland's first [partially free and democratic parliamentary elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contract_Sejm "Contract Sejm") since the end of the Second World War. [Lech Wałęsa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lech_Wa%C5%82%C4%99sa "Lech Wałęsa"), a Solidarity candidate, eventually [won the presidency in 1990](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_Polish_presidential_election "1990 Polish presidential election").[^169] [^170] [^171] The Solidarity movement heralded the [collapse of communist regimes and parties across Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989").[^172]

### Third Polish Republic

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Flowers_in_front_of_the_Presidential_Palace_in_Warsaw.jpg/250px-Flowers_in_front_of_the_Presidential_Palace_in_Warsaw.jpg)

Flowers in front of the Presidential Palace following the death of Poland's top government officials in a plane crash on 10 April 2010

A [shock therapy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shock_therapy_\(economics\) "Shock therapy (economics)") programme, initiated by [Leszek Balcerowicz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leszek_Balcerowicz "Leszek Balcerowicz") in the early 1990s, enabled the country to transform its [Soviet-style](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet-style_socialism "Soviet-style socialism") [planned economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_economy "Planned economy") into a [market economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_economy "Market economy").[^173] As with other [post-communist countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-communism "Post-communism"), Poland suffered temporary declines in social, economic, and living standards,[^174] but it became the first post-communist country to reach its pre-1989 [GDP levels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") as early as 1995, although the unemployment rate increased.[^175] Poland became a member of the [Visegrád Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group "Visegrád Group") in 1991,[^176] and joined [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") in 1999.[^177] Poles then voted to join the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") in [a referendum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_Polish_European_Union_membership_referendum "2003 Polish European Union membership referendum") in June 2003,[^178] with [Poland becoming a full member](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland_in_the_European_Union "Poland in the European Union") on 1 May 2004, following the [consequent enlargement of the union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union "2004 enlargement of the European Union").[^179]

Poland joined the [Schengen Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schengen_Area "Schengen Area") in 2007, as a result of which, [the country's borders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borders_of_Poland "Borders of Poland") with other member states of the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") were dismantled, allowing for [full freedom of movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_movement#European_Union "Freedom of movement") within most of the European Union.[^180] On 10 April 2010, the [President of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland") [Lech Kaczyński](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski "Lech Kaczyński"), along with 89 other high-ranking Polish officials [died in a plane crash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_Polish_Air_Force_Tu-154_crash "2010 Polish Air Force Tu-154 crash") near [Smolensk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smolensk "Smolensk"), Russia.[^181]

In 2011, the ruling [Civic Platform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_Platform "Civic Platform") won [parliamentary elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Polish_parliamentary_election "2011 Polish parliamentary election").[^182] In 2014, the [Prime Minister of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland "Prime Minister of Poland"), [Donald Tusk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Tusk "Donald Tusk"), was chosen to be [President of the European Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council "President of the European Council"), and resigned as prime minister.[^183] The [2015](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Polish_parliamentary_election "2015 Polish parliamentary election") and [2019 elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Polish_parliamentary_election "2019 Polish parliamentary election") were won by the national-conservative [Law and Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_and_Justice "Law and Justice") Party (PiS) led by [Jarosław Kaczyński](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaros%C5%82aw_Kaczy%C5%84ski "Jarosław Kaczyński"),[^184] [^185] resulting in increased [Euroscepticism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euroscepticism "Euroscepticism") and [increased friction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_constitutional_crisis "Polish constitutional crisis") with the European Union.[^186] In December 2017, [Mateusz Morawiecki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mateusz_Morawiecki "Mateusz Morawiecki") was sworn in as the Prime Minister, succeeding [Beata Szydlo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beata_Szyd%C5%82o "Beata Szydło"), in office since 2015. President [Andrzej Duda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrzej_Duda "Andrzej Duda"), supported by Law and Justice party, was re-elected in the 2020 presidential [election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Polish_presidential_election "2020 Polish presidential election").[^187]

As of November 2023, the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine") had led to 17 million [Ukrainian refugees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_refugee_crisis "Ukrainian refugee crisis") crossing the border to Poland.[^188] As of November 2023, 0.9 million of those had stayed in Poland.[^188] In October 2023, the ruling Law and Justice (PiS) party won the largest share of the vote in the [election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Polish_parliamentary_election "2023 Polish parliamentary election"), but lost its majority in parliament. In December 2023, Donald Tusk became the new Prime Minister leading a coalition made up of [Civic Coalition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_Coalition_\(Poland\) "Civic Coalition (Poland)"), [Third Way](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Way_\(Poland\) "Third Way (Poland)"), and [The Left](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Left_\(Poland\) "The Left (Poland)"). Law and Justice became the leading opposition party.[^189]

On 1 June 2025, The Law and Justice candidate for the [2025 Polish presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_Polish_presidential_election "2025 Polish presidential election"), [Karol Nawrocki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karol_Nawrocki "Karol Nawrocki") won the election, beating [Civic Platform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_Platform "Civic Platform") candidate [Rafał Trzaskowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafa%C5%82_Trzaskowski "Rafał Trzaskowski"). The results continued the streak of Law and Justice aligned presidential candidates only losing one presidential election in [2010](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_Polish_presidential_election "2010 Polish presidential election") since its founding in 2001.[^190]

## Geography

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Poland_topo.jpg/250px-Poland_topo.jpg)

Topographic map of Poland

Poland covers an administrative area of 312,722 km <sup>2</sup> (120,743 sq mi), and is the [ninth-largest country in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_area "List of European countries by area"). Approximately 311,895 km <sup>2</sup> (120,423 sq mi) of the country's territory consists of land, 2,041 km <sup>2</sup> (788 sq mi) is internal waters and 8,783 km <sup>2</sup> (3,391 sq mi) is territorial sea.[^191] Topographically, the landscape of Poland is characterised by diverse [landforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landform "Landform"), [water bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrology "Hydrology") and [ecosystems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem "Ecosystem").[^192] The central and northern region bordering the [Baltic Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea") lie within the flat [Central European Plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_European_Plain "Northern European Plain"), but its south is hilly and mountainous.[^193] The average [elevation above the sea level](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Height_above_sea_level "Height above sea level") is estimated at 173 metres.[^191]

The country has a coastline spanning 770 km (480 mi); extending from the shores of the Baltic Sea, along the [Bay of Pomerania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Pomerania "Bay of Pomerania") in the west to the [Gulf of Gdańsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_Bay "Gdańsk Bay") in the east.[^191] The beach coastline is abundant in [sand dune fields](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sand_dunes "Sand dunes") or [coastal ridges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beach_ridge "Beach ridge") and is indented by [spits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spit_\(landform\) "Spit (landform)") and lagoons, notably the [Hel Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hel_Peninsula "Hel Peninsula") and the [Vistula Lagoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vistula_Lagoon "Vistula Lagoon"), which is shared with Russia.[^194] The largest Polish island on the Baltic Sea is [Wolin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolin "Wolin"), located within [Wolin National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolin_National_Park "Wolin National Park").[^195] Poland also shares the [Szczecin Lagoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Szczecin_Lagoon "Szczecin Lagoon") and the [Usedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usedom "Usedom") island with Germany.[^196]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Morskie_Oko_o_poranku.jpg/250px-Morskie_Oko_o_poranku.jpg)

Morskie Oko alpine lake in the Tatra Mountains, part of the Carpathian massif

The mountainous belt in the extreme south of Poland is divided into two major [mountain ranges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_ranges "Mountain ranges"); the [Sudetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudetes "Sudetes") in the west and the [Carpathians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains "Carpathian Mountains") in the east.
