The highest part of the Carpathian massif are the [Tatra Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatra_Mountains "Tatra Mountains"), extending along Poland's southern border.[^197] Poland's highest point is the northwestern summit of [Rysy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rysy "Rysy") at 2,500 metres (8,202 ft) in elevation, located in the Tatras.[^198] The highest summit of the Sudetes massif is [Mount Śnieżka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9Anie%C5%BCka "Śnieżka") at 1,603.3 metres (5,260 ft), shared with the Czech Republic.[^199] The lowest point in Poland situated at [Marzęcino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marz%C4%99cino "Marzęcino") on the [Vistula Fens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vistula_Fens "Vistula Fens"), which is 2.2 metres (7.2 ft) below sea level.[^200]

In Poland, [Trójmorski Wierch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tr%C3%B3jmorski_Wierch "Trójmorski Wierch") is one of the six tripoints of the [European watershed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_watershed "European watershed").

Poland's [longest rivers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rivers_of_Poland "Rivers of Poland") are the [Vistula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vistula_River "Vistula River"), the [Oder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oder_River "Oder River"), the [Warta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warta "Warta"), and the [Bug](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bug_River "Bug River").[^191] The country also possesses one of the highest densities of lakes in the world, numbering around ten thousand and mostly concentrated in the north-eastern region of [Masuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masuria "Masuria"), within the [Masurian Lake District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masurian_Lake_District "Masurian Lake District").[^201] The largest lakes, covering more than 100 square kilometres (39 sq mi), are [Śniardwy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9Aniardwy "Śniardwy") and [Mamry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Mamry "Lake Mamry"), and the deepest is [Lake Hańcza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ha%C5%84cza "Hańcza") at 108.5 metres (356 ft) in depth.[^191]

### Climate

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Poland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/250px-Poland_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png)

Köppen-Geiger climate classification map of Poland

The climate of Poland is [temperate transitional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperateness "Temperateness"), and varies from [oceanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceanic_climate "Oceanic climate") in the north-west to [continental](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_climate "Continental climate") in the south-east.[^202] The mountainous southern fringes are situated within an [alpine climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpine_climate "Alpine climate").[^202] Poland is characterised by warm summers, with a mean temperature of around 20 °C (68.0 °F) in July, and moderately cold winters averaging −1.2 °C (29.8 °F) in January.[^203] In summer, maximum temperatures can reach 40 °C (104.0 °F), while in winter in the Tatra Mountains and Bieszczady Mountains they can even drop below −30 °C (−22.0 °F).

The warmest and sunniest part of Poland is [Lower Silesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Silesia "Lower Silesia") in the southwest and the coldest region is the northeast corner, around [Suwałki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suwa%C5%82ki "Suwałki") and [Olecko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olecko "Olecko") where the climate is affected by [cold fronts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_front "Cold front") from [Scandinavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scandinavia "Scandinavia") and [Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia "Siberia").[^204] [Precipitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precipitation_\(meteorology\) "Precipitation (meteorology)") is more frequent during the summer months, with highest rainfall recorded from June to September.[^205]

There is a considerable fluctuation in day-to-day weather and the arrival of a particular season can differ each year.[^202] [Climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change") and other factors have further contributed to interannual [thermal anomalies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperature_anomaly "Temperature anomaly") and increased temperatures; the average annual air temperature between 2011 and 2020 was 9.33 °C (48.8 °F), around 1.11 °C higher than in the 2001–2010 period.[^204] Winters are also becoming increasingly drier, with less [snowfall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowfall "Snowfall").[^202]

### Biodiversity

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/2020_%C5%BCubry_03.jpg/250px-2020_%C5%BCubry_03.jpg)

The European bison ( żubr ), one of Poland's national animals, is commonly found at the ancient and UNESCO -protected Białowieża Forest.

[Phytogeographically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytogeography "Phytogeography"), Poland belongs to the Central European province of the [Circumboreal Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumboreal_Region "Circumboreal Region") within the [Boreal Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom "Boreal Kingdom"). The country has four [Palearctic ecoregions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palearctic_realm "Palearctic realm") – Central, Northern, Western European [temperate broadleaf and mixed forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest "Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest"), and the [Carpathian montane conifer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpathian_montane_conifer_forests "Carpathian montane conifer forests"). Forests occupy 31% of Poland's land area, the largest of which is the [Lower Silesian Wilderness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Wilderness "Lower Silesian Wilderness").[^206] The most common [deciduous trees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deciduous_trees "Deciduous trees") found across the country are [oak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oak "Oak"), [maple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maple "Maple"), and [beech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beech "Beech"); the most common conifers are [pine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pine "Pine"), [spruce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spruce "Spruce"), and [fir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fir "Fir").[^207] An estimated 69% of all forests are [coniferous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coniferous "Coniferous").[^208]

The [flora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flora "Flora") and [fauna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna_of_Poland "Fauna of Poland") in Poland is that of [Continental Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Europe "Continental Europe"), with the [wisent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_bison "European bison"), [white stork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_stork "White stork") and [white-tailed eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White-tailed_eagle "White-tailed eagle") designated as national animals, and the [red common poppy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Papaver_rhoeas "Papaver rhoeas") being the unofficial floral emblem.[^209] Among the most protected species is the [European bison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_bison "European bison"), Europe's heaviest land animal, as well as the [Eurasian beaver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_beaver "Eurasian beaver"), the [lynx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_lynx "Eurasian lynx"), the [gray wolf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_wolf "Gray wolf") and the [Tatra chamois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatra_chamois "Tatra chamois").[^191] The region was also home to the extinct [aurochs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aurochs "Aurochs"), the last individual dying in Poland in 1627.[^210] Game animals such as [red deer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_deer "Red deer"), [roe deer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roe_deer "Roe deer"), and [wild boar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_boar "Wild boar") are found in most woodlands.[^211] Poland is also a significant breeding ground for [migratory birds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Migratory_birds "Migratory birds") and hosts around one quarter of the global population of white storks.[^212]

Around 315,100 hectares (1,217 sq mi), equivalent to 1% of Poland's territory, is protected within 23 [Polish national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Poland "List of national parks of Poland"), two of which – [Białowieża](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest "Białowieża Forest") and [Bieszczady](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bieszczady_National_Park "Bieszczady National Park") – are [UNESCO World Heritage Sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Poland "List of World Heritage Sites in Poland").[^213] There are 123 areas designated as [landscape parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landscape_Park_\(Poland\) "Landscape Park (Poland)"), along with numerous [nature reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature_reserve "Nature reserve") and other [protected areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Poland "Protected areas of Poland") under the [Natura 2000](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natura_2000 "Natura 2000") network.[^214]
